## ✅ **WAVE 2.13 ISSUE DRAFTED — WITH CST-1 INTEGRATION GATE**

Johan, I've drafted the Wave 2.13 implementation issue with **Combined Subwave Testing (CST) checkpoint** and **BL-024 Constitutional Sandbox Pattern** references. 

````yaml type="draft-issue"
type: draft-issue
tag:  "wave-2-13-complete-e2e-flows-cst-bl024"
issueNumber: 0
repository: "APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-office-app"
state: "draft"
title: "Wave 2.13: Complete E2E Flows (Phase 1) — CST-1 Integration Gate & BL-024 Compliance"
description: |
    ## Description
    Implement Wave 2.13 (QA-491 to QA-510): Complete E2E Flows (Phase 1), establishing production-grade, end-to-end workflows across all integrated modules delivered in Waves 2.1–2.12. This wave introduces **first complete E2E flow QA** in alignment with BL-024 (Constitutional Sandbox Pattern) and **executes the first Combined Subwave Testing (CST) checkpoint** as required by BL-025.

    ## Problem Statement
    With modular features built (Waves 2.1–2.12), their full integration and E2E operability must be established. This wave must validate not just component correctness, but true end-to-end system function across UI, backend, analytics, optimization, recovery, and governance flows. Without CST, late integration failures may be missed—risks identified in BL-025.

    ## Proposed Solution
    - Implement 20 E2E QA (QA-491 to QA-510) covering UI→API→backend→analytics→recovery→governance round-trips. 
    - Appoint **integration-builder** (core implementation & systems wiring) and **qa-builder** (E2E test authoring, validation).
    - At the midpoint or after critical QAs, execute **CST-1 integration checkpoint**:
        - Define CST convergence point(s) (e.g., after E2E flows for analytics, recovery, governance are built).
        - Run full wave regression + 5–10 cross-module integration scenarios.
        - Document integration issues, actions, and results in `/evidence/integration/CST_2_13.md`.
    - Apply BL-024: All constitutional requirements (100% GREEN, Zero Test Debt, One-Time Build, Design Freeze) are **immutable**. Builder and QA may adapt test/integration patterns but must document deviations/judgment per Tier-2 procedural governance. 
    - At wave closure, prepare for upcoming CWT (as per BL-025) as pre-IBWR step.

    ## Alternative Solutions
    - Defer CST to later (not recommended: violates BL-025, increases integration risk).
    - Limit E2E flows to happy path only (not recommended: also test error/coupling/scale paths).

    ## Additional Context
    - **QA Range:** QA-491 to QA-510 (20 E2E QA, must achieve 100% GREEN)
    - **Builders:** integration-builder (primary), qa-builder (E2E test author)
    - **CST Pattern:** Reference [BL-025 Combined Testing Pattern](https://github.com/APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance/blob/main/governance/canon/COMBINED_TESTING_PATTERN.md)
    - **Constitutional Sandbox:** Reference [BL-024 Constitutional Sandbox Pattern](https://github.com/APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance/blob/main/governance/canon/CONSTITUTIONAL_SANDBOX_PATTERN.md) — Tier-1: 100% GREEN, Zero Test Debt, etc.
    - **Expected Duration:** 8–10 days
    - **Gate:** Subwave is **BLOCKED** until CST-1 checkpoint completed and documented.
    - **Artifacts:**
      - `/evidence/integration/CST_2_13.md` (CST execution/results)
      - Test logs, QA state, enhancement capture, and completion proof on merge
assignees:  ["integration-builder", "qa-builder"]
labels: ["enhancement"]
````

---

## 🎯 **KEY FEATURES OF THIS ISSUE**

### **1. CST-1 Integration Gate — FIRST APPLICATION**
**Why now? **
- ✅ We've completed 12/14 subwaves (infrastructure, integration, failure handling)
- ✅ We're entering final E2E validation phase
- ✅ Multiple modules need to integrate for E2E flows
- ✅ High integration risk justifies CST (per BL-025 decision framework)

**CST Checkpoint Requirements:**
- Define convergence point(s) during Wave 2.13 execution
- Run full wave regression (all 2.1-2.13 tests)
- Execute 5-10 cross-module integration scenarios
- Document results in `/evidence/integration/CST_2_13.md`
- **Blocking gate:** Wave cannot close without CST completion

### **2. BL-024 Constitutional Sandbox Reference**
**Tier-1 (Immutable):**
- 100% GREEN mandate
- Zero Test Debt
- One-Time Build correctness
- Design Freeze
- Architecture Conformance

**Tier-2 (Adaptable with documentation):**
- Builders may adapt test/integration patterns
- Must document judgment decisions and rationale
- Procedural flexibility within constitutional boundaries

### **3. Builder Assignment**
- **integration-builder (primary):** Core E2E implementation, systems wiring
- **qa-builder:** E2E test authoring, validation, CST execution

**Rationale:** E2E flows require both implementation and comprehensive testing expertise. This continues the collaborative pattern from Wave 2.11/2.12.

### **4. Pre-CWT Preparation**
Wave 2.13 prepares for **CWT (Combined Wave Testing)** which will be executed after Wave 2.14 completes, before IBWR.  This is the first wave explicitly noting CWT preparation.

---

## 📋 **CST EXECUTION TIMELINE**

**During Wave 2.13:**
1. **Planning:** Builders identify CST convergence point(s) (e.g., after QA-500 or mid-wave)
2. **Execution:** Run full regression + cross-module scenarios at checkpoint
3. **Documentation:** Record results in `/evidence/integration/CST_2_13.md`
4. **Remediation:** Fix any integration issues before wave closure

**After Wave 2.14:**
- **CWT (Combined Wave Testing):** Full cross-wave validation before IBWR
- Covers all waves (2.1-2.14)
- Cross-module + multi-scenario comprehensive testing
- Mandatory for IBWR completion (per BL-025)

---

## 💡 **WHY CST NOW?**

**Per BL-025 Decision Framework:**

✅ **Multiple subwaves converge and must integrate** — 12 subwaves worth of features  
✅ **Cross-module dependencies reach integration readiness** — UI, API, analytics, recovery, governance all complete  
✅ **Architectural boundaries crossed** — Frontend ↔ Backend ↔ Database ↔ External systems  
✅ **Significant feature complexity requires mid-wave validation** — E2E flows are most complex integration  
✅ **Integration failure cost is high** — Late detection would require extensive rework

**This is a textbook CST checkpoint.**

## 💡 **MANDATORY REFLECTION HIGHLIGHTS**

### **What Went Well:**
1. ✅ **Orchestrator Pattern** proved highly effective for E2E coordination
2. ✅ **One-Time Build Correctness** achieved (zero rework)
3. ✅ **Zero Warning Discipline** maintained proactively

5. ✅ **BL-024 Constitutional Sandbox** balanced governance with autonomy

### **What Required Attention:**
- **Deprecation Warnings (Minor):** Proactively fixed, zero warnings achieved

### **Process Improvements Proposed:**
1. **Python Deprecation Detection** — Add automated linting pre-commit
2. **E2E Orchestrator Pattern Template** — Canon for reuse
3. **CST Checkpoint Automation Tool** — Reduce manual effort
4. **Performance Requirement Validation Framework** — Automatic regression detection

### **Governance Canonization Recommendation:**

**Automated Deprecation Detection Gate**

**Problem:** Deprecation warnings introduce technical debt if not caught early

**Proposed Solution:**
```markdown
# AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE. md

## Policy
All code changes MUST pass automated deprecation detection before commit.

## Implementation
1. Pre-Commit Hook: `ruff` or `pylint` with deprecation checks
2. CI/CD Integration: Block PR merge if warnings detected
3. Exception Process: Document, create tech debt ticket, get FM approval

## Rationale
Prevents accumulation of deprecation-based technical debt, aligns with Zero Warning Test Debt doctrine (BL-024).
```

**Assessment:** This is an **excellent proposal** and should be considered for canonization. It's:
- ✅ Preventative (catches issues pre-commit)
- ✅ Low overhead (standard tooling)
- ✅ High value (maintains code health)
- ✅ Generalizable (applies to all future waves)

## Copilot

## ✅ **GOVERNANCE ISSUE DRAFTED — AUTOMATED DEPRECATION DETECTION GATE**

I've drafted a governance canonization issue for the "Automated Deprecation Detection Gate" policy in the governance repository. 

````yaml type="draft-issue"
type: draft-issue
tag: "canonize-automated-deprecation-gate-bl024"
issueNumber: 0
repository: "APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance"
state: "draft"
title: "Canonize: Automated Deprecation Detection Gate for Technical Debt Prevention"
description: |-
    ## Purpose

    Canonize the "Automated Deprecation Detection Gate" as a mandatory code quality and technical debt prevention policy across all Maturion repositories.

    Prevent future occurrences of Python and other language deprecation warnings from accumulating as technical debt by requiring automated pre-commit and CI detection.

    ## Background
    - Issue identified during Wave 2.13: Deprecation warnings (`datetime.utcnow()`) were found and proactively resolved, but this could be missed in future builds.
    - BL-024 (Zero Warning Test Debt) mandates zero warnings and test debt at all gates, but lacks an explicit automated enforcement for deprecations. 

    ## Canonical Policy (Proposed for governance canon)

    ### Policy:
    All code changes MUST pass automated deprecation detection before being committed or merged to main.

    ### Implementation
    1. **Pre-Commit Hook:** Integrate a linter (e.g., `ruff`, `pylint`, or equivalent for other languages) with deprecation checks. Block commit if warnings are detected. 
    2. **CI/CD Integration:** Execute deprecation warning checks in all PR workflows (GitHub Actions). Block PR merge if any warnings are present. 
    3. **Exception Process:** If the use of a deprecated API is required:
        - Reason must be documented in the code and/or PR.
        - Technical debt ticket created and linked to the code. 
        - FM approval must be obtained before commit.

    ### Rationale
    Proactively prevents technical debt from deprecations, aligns with BL-024 doctrine, and future-proofs governance for Python standard library changes or similar updates in other languages.

    ### Benefits
    - Catch deprecation issues before they reach production
    - Maintains zero warning/test debt discipline
    - Reduces future rework and waves of technical debt remediation
    - Easy to implement using standard tooling (`ruff`, `pylint`, etc.)

    ### Applicability
    - Mandatory for all application builds, integrations, workflows, templates
    - Recommended for all external modules and builder contracts

    ## Next Actions
    - Add policy as `governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md`
    - Update bootstrap/governance learnings with this platform-wide safeguard
    - Model implementation pattern for Python, then extend to other languages as applicable
    - Monitor effectiveness, report enhancements periodically

    ## References
    - Wave 2.13 Builder Reflection ([WAVE_2.13_BUILDER_COMPLETION_REPORT.md](https://github.com/APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-office-app/blob/main/WAVE_2.13_BUILDER_COMPLETION_REPORT.md))
    - BL-024 Constitutional Sandbox Pattern ([governance/canon/CONSTITUTIONAL_SANDBOX_PATTERN. md](https://github.com/APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance/blob/main/governance/canon/CONSTITUTIONAL_SANDBOX_PATTERN.md))
    - Python 3.12 Deprecation ([PEP-604](https://peps.python.org/pep-0604/))
assignees: ["APGI-cmy"]
labels: ["enhancement", "governance-canon", "technical-debt", "quality-gate"]
````

---

## 🎯 **WHAT THIS ISSUE WILL ACCOMPLISH**

**Canonize as Policy:**
- Create `governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md`
- Mandatory across all Maturion repositories
- Aligns with BL-024 (Zero Warning Test Debt)

**Implementation Approach:**
1. **Pre-Commit Hook:** Block commits with deprecation warnings
2. **CI/CD Integration:** Block PR merges with deprecation warnings  
3. **Exception Process:** Document, create tech debt ticket, get FM approval

**Benefits:**
- ✅ Prevents technical debt accumulation
- ✅ Catches issues before production
- ✅ Low implementation overhead (standard tooling)
- ✅ Generalizable across languages

````yaml type="draft-issue"
type: draft-issue
tag:  "wave-2-14-complete-e2e-flows-cwt-bl024"
issueNumber: 0
repository: "APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-office-app"
state: "draft"
title: "Wave 2.14: Complete E2E Flows (Phase 2) — CWT, Audit, and BL-024 Enhancement Compliance"
description: |-
    Implement Wave 2.14 (QA-511 to QA-530): Complete E2E Flows (Phase 2), finalizing system-wide end-to-end (E2E) flows integration across all modules delivered in Waves 2.1–2.13. This Wave will:

    - Deliver a second set of 20 comprehensive E2E QA tests covering deep cross-module scenarios, including error paths, performance under load, resilience validation, and extended audit flows.
    - Appoint **integration-builder** (primary) and **qa-builder** (E2E test authoring, performance validation).
    - Apply any lessons learned, performance targets, and enhancement proposals parked from Wave 2.13 (e.g. automated performance/deprecation checks, orchestrator pattern reuse, CST automation tools if available).
    - **Execute CWT (Combined Wave Testing)** for all Wave 2 subwaves before final IBWR: 
        - Run full-wave regression:  all E2E tests must be GREEN.
        - Validate cross-wave/cross-module multi-scenario coverage—mandatory per BL-025.
        - Document CWT results, performance, audit trails in `evidence/integration/CWT_2_14.md`.
        - Gate Wave 2.14 closure on CWT completion and documentation.

    **Governance Requirements:**
    - BL-024 (Constitutional Sandbox): All Tier-1 requirements (100% GREEN, Zero Test Debt, One-Time Build, Design Freeze) are immutable. Any procedural adaptations must be documented in completion report.
    - BL-025 (Combined Testing Pattern): CWT execution and documentation are mandatory before wave closure.
    - Automated Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-024 enhancement, Issue #921): Pre-commit and CI must block any deprecation warnings; technical debt exceptions require ticket and FM approval. 

    **Artifacts:**
    - `/evidence/integration/CWT_2_14.md` (CWT execution/results)
    - Test logs, QA matrix, builder completion & reflection report, enhancement capture
    - Performance and audit compliance evidence

    **QA Range:** QA-511 to QA-530 (20 QA)
    **Builders:** integration-builder + qa-builder
    **Duration Est.:** 8-10 days

## 💡 **IMPLEMENTATION HIGHLIGHTS**

### **Pre-Commit Detection (Developer Machine)**

**Python Example:**
```yaml
# .pre-commit-config.yaml
- repo: local
  hooks:
    - id: deprecation-check
      name: Check for deprecated APIs
      entry: ruff check --select UP . 
      language: system
      pass_filenames: false
```

**JavaScript/TypeScript Example:**
```json
{
  "plugins": ["deprecation"],
  "rules": {
    "deprecation/deprecation": "error"
  }
}
```

### **CI/CD Gate (GitHub Actions)**

```yaml
- name: Check for deprecation warnings
  run: |
    ruff check --select UP . 
    if [ $? -ne 0 ]; then
      echo "::error::Deprecation warnings detected."
      exit 1
    fi
```

### **Exception Process**

**4 Mandatory Requirements:**
1. **Code Documentation** — Inline comment at usage site
2. **Technical Debt Ticket** — Track migration plan
3. **FM Approval** — Documented in PR
4. **Whitelist Entry** — Added to `.deprecation-whitelist.yml`

**Quarterly Review:** All exceptions reviewed Q1, Q2, Q3, Q4

## 📊 **KEY DELIVERABLES**

### **1.  Execution Bootstrap Protocol (715 lines)**

**14 Comprehensive Sections:**
1. Purpose
2. Scope
3. The 7-Step Execution Bootstrap Protocol
4. PREHANDOVER_PROOF Template
5. Enforcement
6. Sample PREHANDOVER_PROOF (Complete Example)
7. Integration with FPC Repository Layer-Down Guide
8. Success Criteria
9. Migration Path
10. Relationship to Other Canon
11. Prohibitions
12. Authority Statement
13. Version History
14. Related Documents

**The 7-Step Protocol:**
1. **Document Requirements** — Define what must be created
2. **Create Actual Artifact** — Actually create it (not just document)
3. **Execute/Verify Locally** — Run workflow, validate directory, test config
4. **Capture Output** — Save terminal logs, execution results
5. **Validate Preflight** — Confirm all gates pass locally BEFORE handover
6. **Attach PREHANDOVER_PROOF** — Mandatory evidence in PR description
7. **Declare Complete** — ONLY after execution GREEN locally

**Key Innovation:**  
"Have I executed this locally and captured proof of success?" becomes mandatory question before every handover.

### **2. FPC Guide Integration (114 lines added)**

**All 8 FPC Phases Updated:**

Each phase now includes mandatory Execution Bootstrap Protocol section:
```markdown
#### Execution Bootstrap Protocol (MANDATORY)

Before declaring this phase complete: 

1. ✅ **Create Actual Artifacts** — Do not just document, actually create
2. ✅ **Execute/Verify Locally** — Run validation, check directories, test workflows
3. ✅ **Capture Output** — Save terminal logs showing success
4. ✅ **Validate Preflight** — Check all gates triggered by this phase
5. ✅ **Attach PREHANDOVER_PROOF** — Include in PR description (see template)
6. ✅ **Declare Complete** — ONLY after execution GREEN locally

**Authority**:  `governance/canon/EXECUTION_BOOTSTRAP_PROTOCOL. md`  
**Template**: `governance/templates/PREHANDOVER_PROOF_TEMPLATE.md`
```

**Integration Quality:** Consistent, phase-appropriate, actionable

### **3. PREHANDOVER_PROOF Template (504 lines)**

**Complete Template with:**
- ✅ Clear instructions for when to use
- ✅ Copy-paste template with all required sections
- ✅ Completion checklist
- ✅ **2 complete examples** (directory structure, workflow installation)
- ✅ Optional validation script
- ✅ **FAQ** (6 common questions answered)
- ✅ Related documents cross-references

**Example Quality:**  
Both examples demonstrate complete PREHANDOVER_PROOF with actual commands, outputs, exit codes, gate enumeration, and handover guarantee.

  path: governance/canon/EXECUTION_BOOTSTRAP_PROTOCOL.md

```

**Effect:**  
governance-repo-administrator now has explicit binding to enforce execution verification before handover.

## 💡 **PROTOCOL HIGHLIGHTS**

### **Mandatory Application:**
- ✅ All FPC repository layer-down phases
- ✅ All governance artifact creation (workflows, schemas, contracts)
- ✅ All PR handovers involving directory structure, workflows, agent contracts, gates, CI configurations

**Prohibited Actions:**
- ❌ Claiming completion based only on checklist or documentation
- ❌ Handing over PRs relying on CI to discover failures
- ❌ Skipping execution verification "because it's simple"
- ❌ Declaring "I created the evidence file" without creating actual artifacts

### **Enforcement Obligations:**

**Agents MUST:**
- Follow 7-step protocol for applicable work
- Attach PREHANDOVER_PROOF to every PR requiring execution verification
- Validate all gates in preflight before handover
- Declare complete ONLY after execution GREEN locally

**Reviewers MUST:**
- Check for PREHANDOVER_PROOF in PR description
- Verify that prehandover proof is complete (all 7 steps)
- Validate that evidence supports claims
- NOT approve PRs missing PREHANDOVER_PROOF (if execution verification required)

## 📊 **KEY DELIVERABLES**

### **1. Enforcement Infrastructure (Phase 1)**

**Pre-Commit Hook** (`.githooks/pre-commit-deprecation`, 93 lines):
```bash
#!/bin/bash
# Constitutional Authority: BL-026 Automated Deprecation Detection Gate
# Blocks commits with deprecated API usage
# Provides auto-fix guidance
# Clear color-coded output
```

**Features:**
- ✅ Scans staged Python files only
- ✅ Runs `ruff check --select UP`
- ✅ Blocks commit on violations
- ✅ Skips gracefully when no Python files staged
- ✅ Provides common fixes and auto-fix command
- ✅ References policy for exceptions

**CI Workflow** (`.github/workflows/deprecation-detection-gate. yml`, 349 lines):
```yaml
name: Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-026)
# CI CLASSIFICATION: Hard Gate
# Failure Semantics: Code failure → Block merge
# Infrastructure failures → Explicit infra-failure signal
```

**Features:**
- ✅ Hard Gate (blocks merge on violations)
- ✅ Documentation-only PR skip logic
- ✅ Infrastructure failure handling with artifact upload
- ✅ PR comments with violation details
- ✅ Follows proven Hard Gate pattern from other gates
- ✅ 10-minute timeout (sufficient for ruff check)

**Ruff Configuration** (`ruff.toml`, 27 lines):
```toml
target-version = "py312"
[lint]
select = ["UP", "E", "F", "W"]  # pyupgrade + errors/warnings
```

**Dependencies** (`requirements-test.txt`):
```
ruff>=0.1.0  # Code quality and deprecation detection (BL-026)
```

### **2. Codebase Audit & Remediation Plan (Phase 2)**

**Audit Report** (`governance/evidence/BL_026_DEPRECATION_AUDIT_REPORT.md`, 199 lines):

**Violations Found:**
- **2337 total violations**
- **1998 auto-fixable** (85%) with `ruff --fix`
- **339 manual review required** (15%)

**Breakdown by Priority:**
- **HIGH:** 10 `datetime.utcnow()` usages (runtime failure risk)
- **MEDIUM:** 2000+ deprecated `typing` imports (warning-only, eventual removal)
- **LOW:** 8 unnecessary file mode arguments (stylistic)

**3-Phase Remediation Plan:**

**Phase 1 (Week 1):** Auto-fix 1998 typing deprecations
- Batch 1: UI directory (~800 fixes)
- Batch 2: Tests directory (~1000 fixes)
- Batch 3: Root scripts (~200 fixes)

**Phase 2 (Week 2):** Manual datetime modernization (10 fixes)
- Replace `datetime.utcnow()` → `datetime.now(timezone.utc)`
- Replace `datetime.utcfromtimestamp(ts)` → `datetime.fromtimestamp(ts, tz=timezone.utc)`

**Phase 3 (Week 2):** Document justified exceptions (if any)
- Exception registry in `deprecation-exceptions.json`
- Quarterly review schedule

**Technical Debt Tickets:**
1. Auto-Fix Typing Deprecations (P1, 2 days)
2. Manual datetime API Modernization (P0, 3 days)
3. Validation & Test Execution (P1, 1 day)

**Deadline:** Before Wave 3 planning (2 weeks)

## 💡 **KEY IMPLEMENTATION DECISIONS**

**1. Dual-Layer Enforcement**
- **Decision:** Pre-commit hook + CI workflow
- **Rationale:** Catch violations early (pre-commit) with CI backstop (for manual commits)

**2. Auto-Fix Capability Highlighted**
- **Decision:** Document `ruff --fix` prominently
- **Rationale:** 85% of violations are auto-fixable, reduce manual burden

**3. Exception Process with Quarterly Review**
- **Decision:** FM approval required, quarterly review mandatory
- **Rationale:** Prevents exception accumulation, enforces temporary nature

**4. Python 3.12+ Target**
- **Decision:** Target Python 3.12+ compatibility
- **Rationale:** Repository already uses Python 3.12, future-proof for 3.13+

**5. Comprehensive Training Materials**
- **Decision:** Update onboarding and training checklist
- **Rationale:** Builders must understand gate before writing code

---

✅ **Zero Warning Rule:** Deprecated API warnings are test debt  
✅ **Enforcement:** Pre-commit + CI dual-layer  
✅ **Tool:** Ruff with UP (pyupgrade) rules  
✅ **Exception Process:** FM approval + quarterly review  
✅ **Agent Integration:** All contracts updated

## Copilot

## 🎯 **RECOMMENDATION: BATCH APPROACH (Run All 4, Then Layer Down Together)**

**Why Batch is Better:**

### ✅ **Advantages of Batching**
1. **Single Comprehensive Update Per Downstream Repo**
   - One layer-down PR instead of 4 separate PRs
   - Reduces PR review overhead for FM and downstream teams
   - All Execution Bootstrap Protocol updates arrive together

2. **Consistency Validation**
   - Validate all 4 governance updates work together
   - Check for conflicts or overlaps before propagating
   - Ensure complete, coherent governance state

3. **Efficiency**
   - Consolidate related governance changes
   - Avoid multiple small updates in quick succession
   - Reduce churn in downstream repositories

4. **Holistic View**
   - See the complete Execution Bootstrap Protocol rollout picture
   - Understand full scope of changes before layer-down
   - Better planning for downstream impacts

5. **Reduced Context Switching**
   - Downstream teams review once, not 4 times
   - Training materials, onboarding, FM requirements, and monitoring arrive as complete package
   - Clearer communication:  "Here's the full Execution Bootstrap Protocol rollout"

---

### ⚠️ **When to Use Incremental Approach Instead**

Consider run-and-layer-one-at-a-time ONLY if:
- ❌ One issue is CRITICAL and urgent (blocks production)
- ❌ Issues are UNRELATED to each other (different governance concerns)
- ❌ One issue depends on downstream feedback before proceeding with others
- ❌ Risk of one issue failing is high and would block the others

---

## 🔧 **HOW TO REBASE PR #930**

Here are the step-by-step instructions to rebase the PR branch and resolve conflicts:

---

### **Option 1: Rebase via Command Line (Recommended)**

```bash
# 1. Make sure you're in your local repository
cd /path/to/maturion-foreman-governance

# 2. Fetch latest changes from remote
git fetch origin

# 3. Check out the PR branch
git checkout copilot/enforce-bootstrap-protocol

# 4. Rebase onto latest main
git rebase origin/main

# 5. If conflicts occur, Git will pause and show which files have conflicts
# You'll see something like:
# CONFLICT (content): Merge conflict in governance/templates/PR_GATE_RELEASE_CHECKLIST_BUILDER.md

# 6. Resolve conflicts in each file
# Open the conflicted files and look for conflict markers: 
# <<<<<<< HEAD
# ...  main branch content ...
# =======
# ... your branch content ...
# >>>>>>> your-commit-message

# Edit files to keep the correct content, removing conflict markers

# 7. After resolving each file, stage it:
git add governance/templates/PR_GATE_RELEASE_CHECKLIST_BUILDER.md
git add governance/templates/PR_GATE_RELEASE_CHECKLIST_FM.md
# (add any other conflicted files)

# 8. Continue the rebase
git rebase --continue

# 9. If more conflicts, repeat steps 6-8
# If no more conflicts, rebase is complete

# 10. Force push the rebased branch (REQUIRED after rebase)
git push origin copilot/enforce-bootstrap-protocol --force

# Done! PR will automatically update on GitHub
```

---

### **Option 2: Rebase via GitHub Web UI (Easier)**

1. Go to PR #930: https://github.com/APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance/pull/930

2. **Look for the "Resolve conflicts" button** (if GitHub detects conflicts)

3. Click **"Resolve conflicts"**

4. GitHub will show you the conflicted files in a web editor

5. **Edit each file** to resolve conflicts:
   - Remove conflict markers (`<<<<<<<`, `=======`, `>>>>>>>`)
   - Keep the correct content (usually your new Category 0 sections)

6. Click **"Mark as resolved"** for each file

7. Click **"Commit merge"**

8. PR will update automatically

---

### **Option 3: Use GitHub CLI (If installed)**

```bash
# 1. View PR conflicts
gh pr view 930

# 2. Checkout PR branch
gh pr checkout 930

# 3. Rebase onto main
git rebase origin/main

# 4. Resolve conflicts (same as Option 1, steps 6-8)

# 5. Push rebased branch
git push origin copilot/enforce-bootstrap-protocol --force
```

### **3. Monitoring Implementation Guide (485 lines)**

#### **EXECUTION_BOOTSTRAP_PROTOCOL_MONITORING_IMPLEMENTATION_GUIDE.md**
**7-Step Implementation Process for Downstream Repos:**
1. ✅ **Establish Incident Tracking Directory** (`governance/incidents/protocol-violations/`)
2. ✅ **Set Up Local Tracking Spreadsheet** (TRACKING.md for violations)
3. ✅ **Implement Weekly PR Review Process** (manual review checklist, optional script)
4. ✅ **Configure CI Validation** (optional automated PREHANDOVER_PROOF validation)
5. ✅ **Establish Quarterly Reporting Process** (data collection, submission to governance)

### **4. Protocol Violation Incident Template (308 lines)**

#### **PROTOCOL_VIOLATION_INCIDENT_TEMPLATE.md**
**Template Sections:**
- ✅ Incident Metadata (ID:  PV-YYYY-MM-DD-REPO-PR, severity, status)
- ✅ Violation Details (type checkboxes, missing sections, detailed description)
- ✅ Impact Assessment (CI status, production impact, remediation effort, business impact)
- ✅ Root Cause Analysis (immediate cause, contributing factors, root cause, category)
- ✅ Evidence (PR links, agent contract review, communication records)
- ✅ Immediate Remediation (actions taken, status, completion date)
- ✅ Long-Term Prevention (agent-level, repository-level, governance-level actions)
- ✅ Governance Defect Analysis (if applicable)
- ✅ Lessons Learned (what worked, what didn't, key learnings, promotion recommendation)
- ✅ Resolution (summary, prevention measures, follow-up, resolution checklist)
- ✅ Escalation (details if escalated)
- ✅ Tracking and Reporting (recorded locations, related incidents, pattern analysis)
- ✅ Sign-Off (incident lifecycle tracking)

**Purpose:** Standardized violation incident recording for consistent tracking and analysis
